    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer7921296915611218289"><b>The dream chooses the dreamer, not the other way around—</b>and Lazlo Strange, war orphan and junior librarian, has always feared that his dream chose poorly. Since he was five years old he’s been obsessed with the mythic lost city of Weep, but it would take someone bolder than he to cross half the world in search of it. Then a stunning opportunity presents itself, in the pers</span>
  <span id="freeText7921296915611218289" style="display:none"><b>The dream chooses the dreamer, not the other way around—</b>and Lazlo Strange, war orphan and junior librarian, has always feared that his dream chose poorly. Since he was five years old he’s been obsessed with the mythic lost city of Weep, but it would take someone bolder than he to cross half the world in search of it. Then a stunning opportunity presents itself, in the person of a hero called the Godslayer and a band of legendary warriors, and he has to seize his chance or lose his dream forever.<br /><br />What happened in Weep two hundred years ago to cut it off from the rest of the world? What exactly did the Godslayer slay that went by the name of <i>god</i>? And what is the mysterious problem he now seeks help in solving?<br /><br />The answers await in Weep, but so do more mysteries—including the blue-skinned goddess who appears in Lazlo’s dreams. How did he dream her before he knew she existed? And if all the gods are dead, why does she seem so real?<br /><br /><i>Welcome to Weep.</i></span>

<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/932769-why-is-the-us-version-have-544-pages-and">Why is the US version have 544 pages and the UK version have 432 pages? I really want to know because I&#39;m tempted to buy the UK version because of that stunning book cover, but if the US version has something like extra content (hence the extra pages) then I might buy both? Please answer soon!</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_932769'><a id="like_count_community_question_932769" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/932769?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">5 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F28449207-strange-the-dreamer">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/932769-why-is-the-us-version-have-544-pages-and">4 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/932769-why-is-the-us-version-have-544-pages-and">See all 6 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/67494663-pete-r"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_100x100-259587f1619f5253426a4fa6fb508831.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/67494663-pete-r">Pete R</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">This has to do with 'leading' (pronounced ledding) which is simply the amount of space between the lines of print. For some reason US publishers conve<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">This has to do with 'leading' (pronounced ledding) which is simply the amount of space between the lines of print. For some reason US publishers conventionally leave more space between the lines and so you get less lines on the same size page which means more pages for the same text. <br /><br />I think this is aesthetic, it makes the page look lighter, less dense, more appealing. <br /><br />Perhaps it also makes reading easier on the eye.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerFooter'>

</div>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });
      $('span_class_gr-hyperlink_sort_order_span_tip_857').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>    </div>
</div>

<div id="review_1897501493" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1897501493" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1897501493?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=signed">signed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=angels">angels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=demons">demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1897501493" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16585346168600169927">Have you ever loved a book so much that it completely fills your soul, warms your heart, and heals your broken pieces? <br/><br/>Because that's <i>Strange the Dreamer</i>.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491963126i/22467313._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“On the second Sabbat of Twelfthmoon, in the city of Weep, a girl fell from the sky. Her skin was blue, her blood was red.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>This is that rare type of book that, while reading, is a constant reminder of why you fell in love with reading in the first place. This book is perfection. This book is a tangible piece of joy. The feeling whil</span>
  <span id="freeText16585346168600169927" style="display:none">Have you ever loved a book so much that it completely fills your soul, warms your heart, and heals your broken pieces? <br><br>Because that's <i>Strange the Dreamer</i>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491963126i/22467313._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“On the second Sabbat of Twelfthmoon, in the city of Weep, a girl fell from the sky. Her skin was blue, her blood was red.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>This is that rare type of book that, while reading, is a constant reminder of why you fell in love with reading in the first place. This book is perfection. This book is a tangible piece of joy. The feeling while reading this is indescribable, but the closest word choice would have to be pure bliss. <br><br>This isn't the type of book to come around often. In fact, the last time I felt this was back in 2015 with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1301719771" rel="nofollow noopener">The Name of the Wind</a>, and the same feeling of guilt from giving other books five star ratings is here again. This book is so much greater than five stars. Yet, this book feels unratable, because how do you rate perfection instead of just feeling at a loss of words because of its awe? <br><br>I don't see how anything I'll read in 2017 can beat this. Not <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1630234463" rel="nofollow noopener">A Court of Wings and Ruin</a>, not <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1767894910" rel="nofollow noopener">Tyrant's Throne</a>, not <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1931515567" rel="nofollow noopener">Skullsworn</a>, not <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1894302078" rel="nofollow noopener">All the Crooked Saints</a>, not <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1835604604" rel="nofollow noopener">The Chosen</a>, not anything. Just throw my 2017 anticipation list away, because <i>Strange the Dreamer</i> was all I needed this year. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Two hundred years ago, there was a storm.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>I truly believe the best way to go into this book is blind, I wouldn't even read the synopsis, but the basic premise of this story is that we are introduced to an orphan, who has always been ostracized for being different, and he is constantly dreaming of the Unseen City that everyone else has long forgotten. He grows up, and moves locations, but the mystery city is always on his mind. Then, he finally gets confirmation that the Unseen City is very real and very much in need of help. <br><br>Surprise mystery after surprise mystery, eloquent word construction after more eloquent word construction, plot twist after plot twist, and you will become so immersed in this world that you will feel like you yourself have lived in the Unseen City all your life. <br><br>I will say that this book does have a really strong romance. In fact, it probably has one of the biggest OTPS I've ever read. Like, I'm real invested. Probably too invested. There is also <i>*gasp*</i> sex in this book, and is dealt with in such a realistic and natural way, while also being very believable, because these characters are seventeen-years-old and are discovering their bodies for the first time. But don't go into this expecting <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1278845732" rel="nofollow noopener">A Court of Mist and Fury</a>'s sex scenes, but go into this knowing that it is an older YA book with mature themes that are amazingly written. Again, I'm too emotionally invested in these fictional characters. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“She asked in a hesitant whisper, “Do you still think I’m a… a singularly unhorrible demon?” “No,” he said, smiling. “I think you’re a fairy tale. I think you’re magical, and brave, and exquisite. And…” His voice grew bashful. Only in a dream could he be so bold and speak such words. “I hope you’ll let me be in your story.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>➽ <b>
  <u>The Plot -</u>
</b> This story is so unique, like, take my breath away, how did a human even come up with this, unique. The themes brought up are so important, and the messages will stick with you. The plot is engaging, addicting, and nothing short of phenomenal. <br><br>➽ <b>
  <u>The Writing -</u>
</b> I kind of want to just write "Laini Taylor is Queen" and leave it at that. The only other person I can compare her writing style to is Maggie Stiefvater. Lyrical writing speaks to my very soul, but Laini Taylor's craft is so perfected that she weaves these heart stopping, unbelievable lines that are so poetic that just leaves me with my mouth open, my breath gone, and my heart pounding. This writing will make you feel as if you are dreaming, and you'll never confuse it with a nightmare. Laini Taylor's writing is a tier above anything I've ever read. Anything.<br><br>➽ <b>
  <u>The World -</u>
</b> Again, like the plot, the world is so unique and so well crafted. The settings are enough to fill even the most empty of hearts. We have libraries, books upon books, story after story, a mysterious city with an even more mysterious water source running underneath it, mythical armies, demons and angels, domination and salvation. And we have magic, and the magic system in this world is a little random, but learning about all the different possibilities was fascinating. Again, something I became addicted over. <br><br>➽ <b>
  <u>The Characters -</u>
</b> <i>*breaks down in tears*</i> I can't. The two main protagonists of this story, Lazlo and Sarai, are everything you could ever want and then more. They are empathetic, helpful, resistant, persistent, hopeful, even in the most bleak of situations, and capable of unconditional love. This story is also filled with gods and goddesses, a lot of ghosts, and maybe a few monsters. Oh, and moths. How I love the moths. <br><br>➽ <b>
  <u>The Messages -</u>
</b> You can take a lot from <i>Strange the Dreamer</i>, but two messages are very predominant throughout this book. The first message is about race and how we treat and blame others dependent on their skin color based on bad things that other people with that skin color have done. Welcome to America, what ban attempt are we up to now? The next message, and the biggest constant theme of this novel, is that we are not our parent's/ancestor's mistakes. Everyone can change and everyone can be/do better. It is never too late to do good. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Sarai was seventeen years old, a goddess and a girl. Half her blood was human, but it counted for nothing. She was blue. She was godspawn. She was anathema. She was young. She was lovely. She was afraid.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>This book is beyond words with its perfection. I loved every aspect of it, and the only legitimate negative thing I have to say is that <i>Strange the Dreamer</i> makes a very unfortunate abbreviation. And as much as that makes me giggle while taking notes, that's honestly it. <br><br>Thank you, Laini Taylor, for a book I will carry in my heart for the rest of my life. This is the best thing I've read in years, and I will never forget this story, these characters, or its message. This book is a love letter to story lovers everywhere, and I recommend this book to everyone with every fiber of my being. Also, I'm buying this for everyone for Christmas, so if you're my friends or family reading this, pretend to be surprised. <br><br>No other title in 2018 will come close to the anticipation I feel for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1958236129" rel="nofollow noopener">The Muse of Nightmares</a>. Please, Lord, help me and my very fragile heart with the wait. <br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany/profile" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a> <br><br><b>[Update: July 26th, 2017]</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1501103860i/23417933._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>You can never have too many copies of your favorite book! 📖🦋✨<br><br><b>[Reread: March, 2018]</b><br>This is still such a masterpiece! I reread this during my Spring break in California and it was nothing short of perfection all over again. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1521852532i/25264363._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="16585346168600169927" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

The Special Edition Illumicrate Box. It's hard to see but this book has Gold Sprayed Edges to go with the cover. We got a few other goodies in the box too as well Muse of Nightmares. I just love my books! ♥</b><br><br><img alt=" " src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1541095850i/26533710._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Audio re-read was freaking awesome! <br><br><b>Had to get the UK Version &amp; my bookmark from my favorite place on Etsy. Yay!</b><br><br><img alt=" " src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1499174378i/23200653._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book is amazing! That's just all there is to it. ❤ Laini Taylor is amaze balls! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1490917019ra/22358506.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When I got this beautiful book from UPS I about fell over. It is so freaking beautiful. The cover is so shiny and no amount of pictures can do it justice. You just have to see it for yourself. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490917019i/22358507._SY540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book is so full of everything. How do I even review a book that is all over and made me sad and took me to a strange and mystical world. <br><br>Lazlo Strange, whom I love, was an orphan boy who went on an errand to The Great Library and never returned. He loved books and was lost in them until he was found and they just kept him on instead of sending him back to the home. He became a librarian. But he was obsessed with the story of Weep and what happened there. He spent years writing his own journals about the place. <br><br>Lazlo was know as "Strange The Dreamer" or Lazlo Strange. But he wasn't strange at all and the things he found out helped him later on. Sometimes dreams can come true. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>I'm going to Weep, he thought, and could have laughed at the pun, but he kept his composure, and when the Tizerkane warriors rode out of the Great Library and out of Zosma, Strange the dreamer went with them.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>I'm not going to give out any kind of spoilers because this is a book you need to discover on your own. It's freaking amaze balls! Did I already say that? <br><br>I will say there are a good bit of characters in the book, nothing confusing, but my favorites are Lazlo and Sarai. ❤<br><br>Laini Taylor can write some beautiful words. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>Weep slept. Dreamers dreamed. A grand moon drifted, and the wings of the citadel cut the sky in two: light above, dark below.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>Sarai is something else but I'm not going to tell you what she is and there are others like her. There is a really sad story behind all of that as well. But Sarai is wonderful and kind and different. <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>Streaming forth into the night, the darkness fractured into a hundred fluttering bits like windblown scraps of velvet. A hundred smithereens of darkness, they broke apart and re-formed and siphoned themselves into a little typhoon that swept down toward the rooftops of Weep, whirling and wheeling on soft twilight wings. <br><br>Sarai screamed moths. Moths and her own mind, pulled into a hundred pieces and flung out into the world.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>Seriously, if you have wanted to get this book, get it and I hope you love it. I didn't understand every little bit about the book but that's okay because I still loved it. ❤<br><br>Of course that ending . . . and there is so much more going on in the book but like I said, you need to read it and feel the magic. I don't even know where Laini Taylor comes up with this stuff. Just the way she writes is surreal. <br><br>Now we have to a wait a billion years to get the next one. *Sob*<br><br>MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2017/03/strange-dreamer-by-laini-taylor.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16326085571171623493" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1497206943" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1497206943" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1497206943?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1497206943" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14766879183424828844"><blockquote>
  <i>It was impossible, of course.<br/>But when did that ever stop any dreamer from dreaming?</i>
</blockquote><br/><b>Oh hell, it was gorgeous perfection</b>.<br/><br/>I've been away for a while because I'm on vacation, but I just had to step back in and review this <b>completely strange, utterly beautiful</b> book. I've been waiting so long for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/324620.Laini_Taylor' title='Laini Taylor' rel='nofollow noopener'>Laini Taylor</a> to steal my heart once more, and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28449207.Strange_the_Dreamer__Strange_the_Dreamer___1_' title='Strange the Dreamer (Strange the Dreamer, #1) by Laini Taylor' rel='nofollow noopener'>Strange the Dreamer</a> does not disappoint.<br/><br/>It's so tempting when reviewing Taylor's books to talk about the writing style and language. Because it's stunning. I </span>
  <span id="freeText14766879183424828844" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>It was impossible, of course.<br />But when did that ever stop any dreamer from dreaming?</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>Oh hell, it was gorgeous perfection</b>.<br /><br />I've been away for a while because I'm on vacation, but I just had to step back in and review this <b>completely strange, utterly beautiful</b> book. I've been waiting so long for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/324620.Laini_Taylor" title="Laini Taylor" rel="nofollow noopener">Laini Taylor</a> to steal my heart once more, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28449207.Strange_the_Dreamer__Strange_the_Dreamer___1_" title="Strange the Dreamer (Strange the Dreamer, #1) by Laini Taylor" rel="nofollow noopener">Strange the Dreamer</a> does not disappoint.<br /><br />It's so tempting when reviewing Taylor's books to talk about the writing style and language. Because it's stunning. I don’t know where the line between purple and beautiful prose should be drawn, but I do know that Laini Taylor stands just on the right side of it. The very sentences themselves <i>feel</i> magical and dreamy, creating an atmosphere that convinces you you've been transported to another world. <br /><br />There's a timeless fairy tale quality to her writing, too; it’s *almost* too much, *almost* too poetic, and yet somehow it is just perfect. I also particularly loved the running theme of dreamers and dreaming here:<br /><blockquote>
  <i>It was why she dared no longer dream: because in her own sleep she was like any dreamer, at the mercy of her unconscious. When she fell asleep, she was no sorceress or dark enthralled, but just a sleeping girl with no control over the terrors within her.</i>
</blockquote><br />Okay, where was I? See what I mean? You can get all caught up in the writing and lose your trail of thought. But my point was that while it's tempting to go on and on about Taylor's writing, it does a disservice to the fantastic storytelling underneath. Because, personally, you can wax poetic until you're blue in the face, but if I'm not interested in the characters and underlying story/conflicts, I'll be left feeling cold.<br /><br />No need to worry about that here.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28449207.Strange_the_Dreamer__Strange_the_Dreamer___1_" title="Strange the Dreamer (Strange the Dreamer, #1) by Laini Taylor" rel="nofollow noopener">Strange the Dreamer</a> opens with the orphaned Lazlo. Though a big dreamer, he is a junior librarian and, let's face it, probably never going to turn his dreams into anything more than just that. Ah, but no! Because this orphan is about to have his life turned upside down when his biggest, wildest dream comes closer than ever before.<br /><br />You see, when Lazlo was young, the name of the lost, mythical city was stolen from everyone's minds. He knows he once knew the Unseen City's real name, but the word left in its place is Weep. No matter how he struggles to remember, all he hears is the same old "Weep". Obsessed with discovering what happened, he spends his adolescence researching the city, trying desperately to find anything about it, longing to one day visit the city himself.<br /><br />And, of course, like all bold dreamers of fantasy, he will get a chance to go on a magical journey and maybe, just maybe, make his dreams come true. I won't give away any more than that. This is a fairly long book and many things happen, but it's best to discover them for yourself and on the author's terms.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28449207.Strange_the_Dreamer__Strange_the_Dreamer___1_" title="Strange the Dreamer (Strange the Dreamer, #1) by Laini Taylor" rel="nofollow noopener">Strange the Dreamer</a> is so unique in its <b>rich world-building, its wonderfully-conceived story of gods, goddesses, ghosts, magic, romance, secrets and guilt</b>, but there is an old tale lurking beneath - that of the orphaned underdog who wanted to be so much more. And whether it is an unloved boy with a scar, stuck in a closet beneath the stairs, who gets to be a powerful wizard, or a nerdy photographer who gets bitten by a spider and learns to be a hero, this is a story that never ceases to appeal to me. <br /><br />How nice it is to be reminded that magic and dreams can come true. With some darkness, nightmares and bloodshed along the way, of course.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14766879183424828844" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1884068774" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1884068774" />
    <a title="Sabaa Tahir" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26226276-sabaa-tahir"><img alt="Sabaa Tahir" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1389816412p2/26226276.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1884068774?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sabaa Tahir" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sabaa Tahir" href="/user/show/26226276-sabaa-tahir">Sabaa Tahir</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1884068774" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6658173873909397019">I love the DoSaB trilogy, which made me nervous to read STRANGE, because how could anything top DoSaB? Somehow, Laini manages it. Probably because she is really, really talented but also I think she might make blood sacrifices to the muses. STRANGE THE DREAMER is a beautiful, unusual, unexpected story which so many great characters that it's very hard for me to pick a favorite. Worldbuilding is intense and wholly original, but still very readable and organic. <br/><br/>The incredible prose made me want to</span>
  <span id="freeText6658173873909397019" style="display:none">I love the DoSaB trilogy, which made me nervous to read STRANGE, because how could anything top DoSaB? Somehow, Laini manages it. Probably because she is really, really talented but also I think she might make blood sacrifices to the muses. STRANGE THE DREAMER is a beautiful, unusual, unexpected story which so many great characters that it's very hard for me to pick a favorite. Worldbuilding is intense and wholly original, but still very readable and organic. <br /><br />The incredible prose made me want to savor every page, but the story hooked me from sentence 1, which made me want to burn through it. In the end, I settled for feverish reading with periods of weeping/prose adoration. I think this was a good system. It's so far my favorite fantasy of 2017, and one of my favs of all time already. Can't wait to read the sequel. Highly highly super YOU MUST READ THIS recommend. </span>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1478148107?book_show_action=true">Dec 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781444788983" href="/book/show/29748925-strange-the-dreamer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=audio-books">audio-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=best-of-2017">best-of-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1478148107" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10776492448337707924"><b>READ #2, Sept 2018</b><br/><br/>Ok but can you just give me a moment while I suffocate with the beauty and perfection that is this book.<b> I haven't had a book totally steal my soul like this in so so long and I am just !!!!! basically fifty million exclamation marks</b>. TheRE IS NO END TO HOW MUCH I LOVE IT. I just...like the foreshadowing, the descriptions, the vivid lush world, the exquisite detail, the myths and legends, the characters who simply do <i>not</i> just stay on a page. They are so so real. <br/><br/>This is the kin</span>
  <span id="freeText10776492448337707924" style="display:none"><b>READ #2, Sept 2018</b><br /><br />Ok but can you just give me a moment while I suffocate with the beauty and perfection that is this book.<b> I haven't had a book totally steal my soul like this in so so long and I am just !!!!! basically fifty million exclamation marks</b>. TheRE IS NO END TO HOW MUCH I LOVE IT. I just...like the foreshadowing, the descriptions, the vivid lush world, the exquisite detail, the myths and legends, the characters who simply do <i>not</i> just stay on a page. They are so so real. <br /><br />This is the kind of book you read and fall completely into.<br /><br />And I shan't come out yoU CANNOT MAKE ME. [insert some wild sobbing here]<br /><br />Anyway, hi, I am wrecked and ready for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25446343.Muse_of_Nightmares__Strange_the_Dreamer___2_" title="Muse of Nightmares (Strange the Dreamer, #2) by Laini Taylor" rel="nofollow noopener">Muse of Nightmares</a>. But also not ready because I can't feel my heartbeat as is??? Holy afjdkslad I am ablaze with how incredibly told this is. (Also I still have only read it via audio! Best decision!) And doubly also I feel many many things for Minya and none of them are hate so ¯\_(ツ)_/¯ excuse me while I go die.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Read #1: April 2018</u>
</b><br /><b>I TRULY DO NOT HAVE WORDS FOR HOW MUCH BEAUTIFUL PERFECTION THIS BOOK IS.</b> I need more stars to give it omg. I honestly feel like this is the most <i>beautifully</i> written book of ever....the words!??? The marvellous exquisite combination of words just!???? IT SLAYED ME. It's all gods and monsters and librarians and the most lush and gorgeous dream landscapes and I cannnnn't. I just can't with <b>how wholly i loved it.</b> I got to this point reading it and was just like "I never want this book to end thanks."<br /><br /><b>OKAY BUT CAN WE TALK ABOUT LAZLO STRANGE FOR A MINUTE?!?</b> Aka the most precious hufflepuff in existence. He is so <i>sweet</i> and pure and good and lovely and jfadskaldjaklj. I love him. I love how his nose got broken by a fairy tale book and that he'll walk into a wall because he's reading so much and how his whole life is about fantastical lost cities and how he dreams the most beautiful and gorgeous dreams the world has ever known. <b>HE IS PERFECT.</b> And relatable. Because book lover. And also 10/10 for how dorky he was.<br /><br />The world doesn't deserve the preciousness of Lazlo Strange.<br /><br />(Also his name is so fabulous.)<br /><br />(Also he dreams himself dragon wings so also I am Lazlo Strange.)<br /><br /><b>And I absolutely adored Sarai too, who is a blue-skinned godspawn.</b> She's hiding from the world that wants her dead because of her horrifically cruel goddess mother. But she is pURE and gOOD too. And I just want to give her a cake. She hasn't had a cake in year and goddammit please someone give Sarai a cake.<br /><br /><b>But what really caught me is the writing.</b> Usually I would be dead with so much flowery prose but I <i>wasn't.</i> I absolutely loved it. It totally swallowed my MIND and I just couldn't stop thinking "I wnat to live in this book." Every word was so perfectly chosen that I was <i>devoured</i> by the story. I've never <i>seen</i> a city so clearly as I see Weep. I THINK LAINI TAYLOR MIGHT BE ABLE TO DO TRUE MAGIC. JUST SAYIN'.<br /><br /><b>This is all about magic and gods and monsters</b> which is 100000% my kind of story. Also dEATh and destruction and psychotic little girls who catch ghosts and legends inside legends and great monsters and beasts and cruel pasts and terrified warriors and god slayers and quiet librarian boys and falling girls with flowers in their hair and -- I JUST -- AJFKDLSAFDJKJKDFSJ.<br /><br /><b>I do think it's not YA though.</b> I read a fair bit of adult fantasy and this read <i>far</i> more like adult. Plus Lazlo is like 20, so.<br /><br /><b>And there were a few things that weren't my favourite but I'm kind of like "OH WHO CARES I STILL ADORE IT WITH ALL MY SOCKS" to the situation.</b> But:<br />• it is rather omnipresent so head-bopping happened a <i>lot</i><br />• and it has a pretty smack-in-the-face dose of instalove<br />• except i ship it so bad jafdksld help me<br /><br /><b>SPOILERS ABOUT LAZLO:</b><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[So I don't even mind that he turned out to be a Special Snowflake™ even though that trope is usually so annoying. Buuuuut, IT'S LAZLO. HE IS KING OF ALL THINGS BEAUTIFUL ANYWAY. But omg that <i>ending</i>. Like he's Scathesus son (shh I can't spell anything; I listened to an audio) and he and Minya are totally going to lock heads right?!? And Lazlo is going to become the god of doom that everyone fears?!?<br /><br />I CAN'T EVEN.<br /><br />I NEED THE SEQUEL. *SOBS*<br /><br /><b>Also I lowkey thought that now that Sarai is dead that Thyron Nero and Lazlo can get together.</b> Haha hahahahahah. #sorry But they would be my secondary ship still.<br /><br />I'm still devastated about Sarai though!! DEVASTATED. But yet pleased because books tend to cushion harsh endings but yaaaaas we got our feels ripped out and everything is horrible and her death was just the most CRUSHING THING OF EVER AND I THINK MY HEART BLED WITH LAZLO'S.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><br /><b>You know? I could just flail forever over how much I loved it.</b> I don't even think you should know too much about the storyline, because it's pure perfection to watch it unravel with Lazlo. &lt;3 But honestly I want to read more books with sweet boys and nightmare girls. I want more books that melt my soul with the most fantastically marvellous writing in the world. <b>I want books that make me DREAM and be inspired to greatness.</b> I FEEL LIKE WRITING A THOUSAND FAIRY TALES AND CONQUERING THE MOON AND FLYING AWAY ON DRAGON WINGS NOW. And a book that steals your heart and your imagination is the <i>perfect</i> kind of book.<br /><br />#obsessed<br /><br /><br /><b>NOTE:</b> I listened to the audiobook and it worked SO well for me. Usually I read too fast, so I think I woudn't have appreciated the lush detailed writing if I hadn't have gone with the audio. Plus it's Steve West who has a gorgeous accent omg. &lt;3 (And narrated The Scorpio Races as Sean so excuse me while Sean and Lazlo are the same and I'm in love.) (But also I listen to it on 2 x the speed ahem. Otherwise I would've lost at least 87 braincells at how slow he reads.)</span>

<div id="review_1596659741" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1596659741" />
    <a title="Warda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30036082-warda"><img alt="Warda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593385153p2/30036082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1596659741?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Warda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Warda" href="/user/show/30036082-warda">Warda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781444788983" href="/book/show/29748925-strange-the-dreamer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=reread-worthy">reread-worthy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=re-reads">re-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=characters-of-colour">characters-of-colour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=i-fell-in-love">i-fell-in-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1596659741" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6409491563351078259">This was a dream to reread. <br/><br/>—————————<br/><br/>I'm thinking about how to review this and honestly, words fail me, so this'll be an attempt. I mean, I will try and somewhat make this cohesive. But nothing will do it justice. You will have to discover the story for that. <br/><br/>This book made me feel hopeful. Validated my views and feelings I’ve always known to be true to my own self. Then Laini Taylor comes along and drops this bomb of a magic on us and my feelings were cemented by a ten-fold.<br/><br/>Lazlo Strange is a b</span>
  <span id="freeText6409491563351078259" style="display:none">This was a dream to reread. <br /><br />—————————<br /><br />I'm thinking about how to review this and honestly, words fail me, so this'll be an attempt. I mean, I will try and somewhat make this cohesive. But nothing will do it justice. You will have to discover the story for that. <br /><br />This book made me feel hopeful. Validated my views and feelings I’ve always known to be true to my own self. Then Laini Taylor comes along and drops this bomb of a magic on us and my feelings were cemented by a ten-fold.<br /><br />Lazlo Strange is a bookworm. A librarian and a dreamer at heart. His fascination with a lost city has been his driving force for the majority of his life. Growing up as an orphan in a city that didn’t really accept him, that is what he became fixated on. He lived and breathed books and learning about the city and wonders of Weep.<br /><br />The way his character was fleshed out was simply stunning. It wasn't just fleshed out; every emotion and thought process the character could have possibly experienced was laid out. Similarly, the same attentive care and focus was given to the other incredible characters and their world, fed to us bit by bit and it beautifully came together, piece by piece. It allowed me to savour the story, enjoy the dream I was living in for a while and experience it in its full glory.<br /><br />This is the sort of writing style that demands and deserves attention. It is not to be rushed, and I don’t think the reader them self would want to rush it. Taking your time with it and revelling in its lushness is when the magic happens.<br />As soon as I entered the story, I was immediately swept away by the language, the intricacy. The attention to detail is mind-blowing and I couldn't help but have such deep admiration for Laini Taylor. I was dreaming whilst reading, building the fantasy up in my head, wandering around in that world that felt so alive to me.<br /><br />One of the main aspects of the book that I absolutely appreciated was how it looked at the concept of dreams. There’s always this debate as to whether it is healthier to be realistic or be a dreamer when it comes to ones goals as dreamers themselves are looked as… ‘lazy’. <br />But this book was based on a dreamer and his dream. How he wished, hoped and how much of that dream encompassed his life and regardless of whether people were dismissing it, he stayed true to his belief and did not doubt it. Yes, the occasional doubt was there, naturally it would be, but his belief in that dream kept him afloat. And that just hit so close to home for me.<br /><br />I want to say more about this book. I want to be able to explain the absolute magic it encompassed and honed within me, the comforting emotions I was feeling throughout and the false sense of security I was duped into believing and led to, because that ending was just heart-wrenching. But I actually can’t. <br /><br />It’s a story I’ll always revisit. . <br /><br />———————————————-<br /><b>INITIAL REACTION! </b><br /><br />Well, fuck. I think my soul has just left my body. RTC when it decides to join me again. <br /><br />———————————————-<br /><b>READING RAMBLES.</b><br /><br />Okay, I'm feeling guilty for having to put this book down for the 2nd time now. 😖😖😖 <br />In no way is it bad. At all. 'Bad' and 'Laini Taylor' don't exist in the same universe, but I haven't touched this book for a month and it's mainly due to the fact that I haven't been in the mood to read fantasy for so long. 😩 Soon, babe. I'll get to you soon. <br /><br /><br />-----------------------------------------------------<br /><br />I'm putting this book down for now, because I'm feeling disgustingly slumpish and Laini Taylor's stories do not deserve this sloppy attention I am giving it right now.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6409491563351078259" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2423350970" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2423350970" />
    <a title="Emma Giordano" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano"><img alt="Emma Giordano" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569693958p2/30604861.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2423350970?book_show_action=true">Aug 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Giordano" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Giordano" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano">Emma Giordano</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2423350970" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6190467512505741513">4.5 stars!! Wow this book truly blew me away!!!<br/><br/>I avoided reading <i>Strange The Dreamer</i> for a <b>looooongggg</b> time. I have a record of epic high fantasy with lyrical prose not sitting well with me and combined with my inability to grasp the synopsis before reading, I was greatly intimidated by this book. How glad I am that I finally gave it a chance and took my time with it because I can't imagine having not experienced this story!</span>

<div id="review_1882092720" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1882092720" />
    <a title="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink"><img alt="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568991289p2/50044222.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1882092720?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" href="/user/show/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink">Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=arcs-i-ve-reviewed">arcs-i-ve-reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=2017-anticipated-reads">2017-anticipated-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1882092720" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17093948984079680181">*Full Review Update*<br/><br/>I honestly still don't know what to rate this, so I'm going with 3.5 stars. <br/><br/>Wow, so it took me nearly two months to finish this book. Here's the thing. The writing quite literally slays, and so does the characterization. My struggle was this: Half the time, I was sitting there in awe, thinking 'This is the best book EVER WRITTEN' ahhh. The other half? I could barely get through a page before falling asleep. There would be pages and pages of descriptions - and while they were </span>
  <span id="freeText17093948984079680181" style="display:none">*Full Review Update*<br /><br />I honestly still don't know what to rate this, so I'm going with 3.5 stars. <br /><br />Wow, so it took me nearly two months to finish this book. Here's the thing. The writing quite literally slays, and so does the characterization. My struggle was this: Half the time, I was sitting there in awe, thinking 'This is the best book EVER WRITTEN' ahhh. The other half? I could barely get through a page before falling asleep. There would be pages and pages of descriptions - and while they were mind-blowing, I was dyyinggg for the story to start.<br /><br />So just a heads up - it takes about halfway or maybe even more for anything to even start happening. The pace didn't pick up until like 80%. <br /><br />My recommendation? If you're a writer (or aspiring writer) - this is a must read. For sure. But be prepared going into it. I think I've highlighted half the book because of how pretty and raw the sentences were. It was poetic at times and short and raw at others. Such an interesting combination I feel like I've learned a ton and I owe Laini a great deal for that.<br /><br />Lazlo Strange is easily one of the most tender and relatable characters in YA lit. He was precious down to the bone, and I swear I don't think anyone could read about him and not fall in love. From the very first page, too. He sucks you in quick. His fascination of 'Weep' becomes the reader's fascination of weep. It's impossible not to feel Lazlo's emotions.<br /><br />As far as the other characters - same deal. They all felt real. I loved Sarai even though she didn't have a huge personality. Her abilities are super dark but super cool and I was totally rooting for her. I also liked to see the interaction with the other... 'gods' or whatever they were. I love how they each had distinguishable personalities. What I didn't love? Their POV talking about next to nothing. <br /><br />Anyway, like I said, the pacing is extremely slow and I think the characters are the entire reason I stuck around. If it hadn't been for them, I would have just picked it up occasionally to get some writing inspiration.<br /><br />The world building was also phenomenally done, (albeit weird at times with the metal thing). But cool. Okay, does anyone remember watching 'The Little Princess' as a kid? That movie was what spurred my obsession with Indian Folklore. I would chain watch that movie over and over again because of the blue goddess love story and ahhhh this book brought back memories of that and of other stories I used to love. Ugh see? This is my issue. I would have loved this book so much more -perhaps even cried over it- if the pacing had been better. <br /><br />So here I sit with mixed feelings. So much greatness. So much brilliance. And yet it took me months to get through it.<br /><br />Take what you will from that! <br /><br /><a href="http://www.herbookishthings.com" rel="nofollow noopener">My Blog</a> ~ <a href="https://www.instagram.com/reverieandink/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> ~ <a href="https://twitter.com/reverieandink" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> ~ <a href="https://www.etsy.com/shop/reverieandink" rel="nofollow noopener">Etsy</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17093948984079680181" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2470525455?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer9756044467390393758"><blockquote>
  <i>“Beautiful and full of monsters?"<br/><br/>“All the best stories are.” </i>
</blockquote>Love that feeling when you start a series and immediately realize <b>there's no going back</b> to normal.<br/><br/>Actual footage of me entering this fandom:<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1536073961ra/26251706.gif' width='300' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>There were <b>
  <u>SO</u>
</b> many elements of this story that really worked for me <i>
  <b>(MINUS THE SO-CALLED LOVE!!!)</b>
</i><br/><br/>Lazlo Strange, an orphaned child, was always fascinated by <b>tales of the missing city </b>- he would make-believe all sorts of adventures. <br/><br/>One day, while playing alone in the monastery orchard, s</span>
  <span id="freeText9756044467390393758" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“Beautiful and full of monsters?"<br><br>“All the best stories are.” </i>
</blockquote>Love that feeling when you start a series and immediately realize <b>there's no going back</b> to normal.<br><br>Actual footage of me entering this fandom:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1536073961ra/26251706.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There were <b>
  <u>SO</u>
</b> many elements of this story that really worked for me <i>
  <b>(MINUS THE SO-CALLED LOVE!!!)</b>
</i><br><br>Lazlo Strange, an orphaned child, was always fascinated by <b>tales of the missing city </b>- he would make-believe all sorts of adventures. <br><br>One day, while playing alone in the monastery orchard, something <b><i>wondrous</i> and<i> terrible </i></b>happened.<br><br> The name of the city was snatched out of his head and replaced with <b>
  <i>Weep.</i>
</b><br><br>He spends every waking moment obsessed with finding out what happened - when suddenly, years later, someone from that very city visits...<br><br>Lazlo sacrifices everything to follow that man back to the city of Weep - <b>it's not every day that your dreams come true.</b><blockquote>
  <i>It was impossible, of course. But when did that ever stop any dreamer from dreaming.</i>
</blockquote>Meanwhile, <b>Sarai is Godspawn </b>- child of the immortal and mortal - only years ago, the mortals rebelled and slain every last God and Godspawn...or so they thought.<br><br>Sarai and her other Godspawn spent the last few decades hiding on the floating city. They were children, still in their diapers when<b> the great slaughter</b> happened.<br><br>She spent her childhood half-staved, <b>unbearably isolated</b> and completely on their own.<br><br>She's a teenager, along with the other surviving Godspawn, and it's becoming<b> increasingly difficult to hide their presence...</b>especially when the humans are bound and determined to take down the floating city.<br><br><b>A chance encounter between Lazlo and Sarai sparks something that neither of them could ever have anticipated...</b><br><br>Overall - this one swept me off of my feet. <br><br>I loved the <b>wild and whimsical world </b>Liani Taylor created - the odd magic, the alien-ness of the Godspawn, the simple joys of Lazlo the librarian-turned-adventurer.<br><br>The only thing that threw me out of this novel was the love -<b> it was absolutely terrible.</b><br><br>If the rest of the book wasn't so good, I would've one-starred this one based on the awful love story.<br><br>Most of the book centers around backstory of both Lazlo and Sarai and how they came to be in the same city. <br><br>Then, they make eye-contact in a dream <b>- BOOM - </b>eternal love and devotion. <br><br>It's just like...come on. Taylor wrote such a <b>rich, complex and absolutely beautiful</b> story...and then throws together a half-assed "love" story.<br><br>It's like, she got to almost the end and was like, "oh sh*t. I forgot to make the characters fall in love. Where's my shoe-horn?"<br><br>Did I mention that the romance "develops" over the course of two nights -<b> entirely through dreams?</b> Without seeing that relationship build, it just seems eye-rollingly-ridiculous. <br><br>Really put me off of reading the second book. I'll still read it, because I'm in love with this amazing world, but I am crossing my fingers that<b> the romance calms itself down.</b><br><br><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br>Extremely well-read by Steven West - the audio really enhanced the novel! <br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br><br>Happy Reading!<br></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2069066303" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2069066303" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2069066303?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/29486766-strange-the-dreamer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale?shelf=fantasy-series">fantasy-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2069066303" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10600202674456233997"><i>“You’re a storyteller. Dream up something wild and improbable," she pleaded. "Something beautiful and full of monsters."<br/>“Beautiful and full of monsters?"<br/>“All the best stories are.”</i><br/><br/>This quote is basically a short summary of the entire book because <b>“Strange the Dreamer”</b> is indeed a story about something beautiful and full of monsters. Well, actually some might even say it’s a story about <u>
  <b>“beautiful monsters"</b>
</u> and you certainly would be more than just right to put it that way. ;-)<br/><br/>Those beautiful</span>
  <span id="freeText10600202674456233997" style="display:none"><i>“You’re a storyteller. Dream up something wild and improbable," she pleaded. "Something beautiful and full of monsters."<br />“Beautiful and full of monsters?"<br />“All the best stories are.”</i><br /><br />This quote is basically a short summary of the entire book because <b>“Strange the Dreamer”</b> is indeed a story about something beautiful and full of monsters. Well, actually some might even say it’s a story about <u>
  <b>“beautiful monsters"</b>
</u> and you certainly would be more than just right to put it that way. ;-)<br /><br />Those beautiful monsters appear in all different kinds of shapes and forms and no matter how hard I would try, I’m convinced I still wouldn’t be able to express how much I loved to read this book. It was magical, it was moving, it was so very different than anything else I’ve ever read. Laini Taylor’s writing is like poetry and it drew me in and left me wanting for more. This world was so intriguing, it’s characters so flawed and mysterious and it’s power so raw. There was so much pain, mistrust, hate, despair and fear. But there was also hope, trust, the flutter of wings, dreams and love. Always love. <br />Desperate love, hopeless love, guilty love, unrequited love, motherly love, hopeful love, destructive love, young love, old love, dying love, love in every form. <br /><br />I think I could go on and on with this one. *lol* Suffice it to say that it was wonderful to read, amazing to experience and heart-breaking to witness. Such a perfect book… such a compelling story. Well done, Laini. Well done! &lt;3<br /><br /><b>The Plot:</b><br /><br /><i>”There were two mysteries, actually: one old, one new. The old one opened his mind, but it was the new one that climbed inside, turned several circles, and settled in with a grunt – like a satisfied dragon in a cozy new lair. And there it would remain – the mystery, in his mind – exhaling enigma for years to come.”</i><br /><br />This quote is everything you’ll get from me when it comes to the plot, because it’s so complex I couldn’t write a summary without giving away some major spoilers. ;-) All I can say is: Read the book. Just read it. I’m sure it will blow your mind. XD<br /><br /><b>The Characters:</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>And here it is, my infamous spoilery spoiler section. XD If you haven’t read the book yet and don’t want to be spoiled you should leave now. If you already read the book and want to hear my thoughts: Welcome to the lion’s den. *lol* Take a seat and a cookie. ;-P</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>Lazlo:</b><br /><br /><i>”The library knows its own mind,” old Master Hyrrokkin told him, leading him back up the secret stairs. “When it steals a boy, we let it keep him.”<br />Lazlo couldn’t have belonged to the library more truly if he were a book himself.</i><br /><br />This boy is so sweet, innocent, amazing and pure. Seriously, I think he might be the purest soul I ever had the pleasure to read about. I love him, I just love him so much!! &lt;33 Lazlo is one hell of a precious bean and all I wanted to do was to protect him from every possible threat and harm that might come his way. He needs to be protected at all costs!!! I mean he’s basically a unicorn and unicorns need to be happy and safe! I just loved how he always tried to see the good in people, how he gave them everything and didn’t even expect anything in return. He was so altruistic and generous it was so beautiful to watch. He never judged. He just listened to all the different sides and he accepted every opinion even if his own differed. In short: If the world would have more Lazlo Strange’s then it definitely would be a better place. =)) Which is the reason why I’m so damn worried about him right now. That ending!!! T_T I really hope he won’t lose his innocence…. Please Laini, let him be okay, don’t allow Minya to corrupt him and to turn him into something bad. *sobs*<br /><br /><i>”If the dream chose the dreamer, then his had chosen poorly. It needed someone far more daring than he. It needed the thunder and the avalanche, the war cry and the whirlwind. It needed fire.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Who had ever expended so much passion on a dream, only to stand helpless as it was granted to others? Others, moreover, who had expended no passion on it at all. His impossible dream had, against all probability, crossed deserts and mountains to come to Zosma and extend an unprecedented invitation.<br />But not to him.”</i><br /><br /><i>”He had loved the library, and had felt, as a boy, as though it had a kind of a sentience, and perhaps loved him back. But even if it was just walls and a roof with papers inside, it had bewitched him, and drawn him in, and given him everything he needed to become himself.”</i><br /><br /><b>Sarai:</b><br /><br /><i>I kiss dozens of people every night.” And she touched a spot just above the outer curve of one cinnamon eyebrow. “Right here. Men and women, babies and grandparents. I kiss them and they shudder.” Her voice was like ice, and so were her hearts. “I kiss them and they grieve.”</i><br /><br />She was such a strong character! I loved that Sarai was so empathic and thought out of the box. After everything she went through she still stood by her convictions and refused to give herself to hatred and wrath. I think it’s admirable that she tried to understand the citizens of Weep and dared to hope that peace was possible. I mean she knew that both sides did awful things, but she was also aware that it were mistakes and atrocities other people had done. She was nothing but a baby when the gods fell and even though Minya kind of bullied her into hurting the people of Weep she still knew that her actions were wrong. She wanted to stop the destructive cycle of hate, mistrust, prejudices and fear and I’m sure if the ending wouldn’t have happened Lazlo and her might have even had a realistic chance to succeed. *sighs* <b>Gosh, I hate that ending! Did I already mention that I hate that ending?</b> &gt;_&lt;<br /><br /><i>”Sarai wasn’t going to kill anyone. She was stubborn, very, and she wasn’t about to surrender her decency or mercy for a sound day’s sleep. She wouldn’t beg Minya for lull. Whatever happened she would never again serve Minya’s twisted will.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Good people do all the things bad people do, Lazlo. It’s just that when they do them, they call it justice.” She paused. Her voice grew heavy. “When they slaughter thirty babies in their cradles, they call it necessary.”</i><br /><br /><b>Eril-Fane:</b><br /><br /><i>”Even after all these years, the thought of Isagol the Terrible stirred such a storm in him – of rancor and longing, desire and disgust, violence and even affection – all of it seething and bleeding and writhing, like a pit of rats eating one another alive. That was what his feelings were now, what Isagol had made of them. Nothing good or pure could survive in him. All was corruption and gore, suffocating in his self-loathing. How weak he was, how pitiful. He might have killed the goddess in the end, but he wasn’t free of her, and he never would be.”</i><br /><br />Ohh Eril-Fane, the guy with one of the coolest nicknames in all history. Godslayer. Sounds awesome! Has a certain ring to it, right? If you consider what had to happen to get that nickname it’s not that cool anymore though. Well, actually it loses all its glory. Boy, was he a tormented and tortured soul. I loved it! *lol* Yeah, I know you might roll your eyes now and say: Gin, why do you always love those flawed characters and villains? The answer is simple. They are complex, they are interesting, and they intrigue me. Immensely I might add. ;-P So back to Eril-Fane. What a fascinating personality. Devoured by rancor and love, torn between duty and self-hatred, eroded by years of shame and despondency, eaten by guilt and longing. Ahh, what’s not to love? *lol* He’s everything I want in a character and Laini Taylor wrote him so well! I just want more of him and I can’t wait for book two!! <br /><br /><i>”Eril-Fane had his own arsenal of horrors; he hardly needed hers. Fear was the last of it. Sarai hadn’t understood before that fear could be the lesser torment. It was shame that tore him apart. It was despair. There was no darkness she could send him to rival what he’d endured already. He had lived three years with Isagol the Terrible. He had survived too much to be driven mad by dreams.”</i><br /><br /><i>”He loved her so much,” she whispered. “It was all a lie. It was a violation. But it didn’t matter, did it, because when Isagol made you feel something, it became real. He hated her. And he loved her. And he killed her.”</i><br /><br /><i>”He looked him right in the eyes and saw a man who was great and good and human, who had done extraordinary things and terrible things and been broken and reassembled as a shell, only then to do the bravest thing of all: He had kept on living, though there are easier paths to take.”</i> <br /><br /><b>Minya:</b><br /><br /><i>”They were all I could carry. They were all I could carry.”<br />There was no echo, no reverberation. If anything, the room ate sound. It swallowed her voice, her words, and her eternal, inadequate apology. But not her memories. She would never be rid of those.”</i> <br /><br /><b>I FREAKING HATE MINYA!!!</b> There, I said it, it’s out now! I understand why she is so angry at the people of Weep and I can see why she’s craving for revenge but I do <b>
  <u>NOT</u>
</b> understand why she has to use other people in order to get what she wants. To turn on Sarai and Lazlo? That’s where I draw the line. No matter how much I’m sorry for what she experienced and how much it hurt and shaped her; I still can’t forgive her what she did in the end!! I mean Sarai is her family, she doesn’t know Lazlo, okay, but Sarai?! She raised her!!! She rescued her and took care of her over those years. She’s basically like a mother figure even though she’s barely a few years older and still looks like a child. Minya is so wrathful and embittered that she sees nothing but hatred and vengeance and even though I know that she’s pulling the strings right now, I still hope that Lazlo and Sarai won’t end up being her puppets. =(( URGH I just dislike her so much! T_T<br /><br /><b>The ships:</b><br /><br /><u>Sarai &amp; Lazlo:</u><br /><br /><i>”There was no one behind her. There was no one else at all. The whole dream shrank to a sphere around the pair of them, and there could be no question that the witchlight was for her, or that it was her he meant when he whispered, with vivid and tender enthrallment, “Who are you?”</i><br /><br />Those two were so damn cute together!!! GAH! I can’t even. From the very first moment they met up until to their dream dates they were just perfection! I loved how hard they fell for each other and yes, I know that was kinda insta-lovey but it was executed so damn well. I mean sometimes this just happens. You meet someone and you fall head over heels. You don’t question if it’s too fast, you don’t think about the future, you just live in the moment and breathe every second you’re in that persons proximity. They give you life, they make you happy, they cause you to wear a permanent grin on your face. And BOY did Laini Taylor do a good job at conveying that feeling! It felt like I was with them, falling in love too. &lt;3 <b>BUT</b> that damn ending!!! ARGH!!! I hate Minya for being so cruel, I hate that the citadel lost balance… I just hate everything that happened in those last few chapters. T_T I want them to be happy but I don’t see how this can work out good… I mean Sarai is basically Minya’s hostage now and Lazlo loves her so much. The next book is going to hurt. This just broke my heart… &gt;_&lt; *sobs*<br /><br /><i>”I think you are a fairy tale. I think you’re magical, and brave, and exquisite. And … “ His voice grew bashful. Only in a dream could he be so bold and speak such words. “I hope you’ll let me be in your story.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Lazlo did hold Sarai in his arms that night, and she was real and flesh, blood and spirit, but not laughter. Not breath. Those had left her body forever.<br />The Muse of Nightmares was dead.”</i><br /><br /><u>Azareen &amp; Eril-Fane:</u><br /><br /><i>”She curved herself against his back, laid her face to the side of his neck, and wept the tears that he could not. Eril-Fane shuddered as her tears seared his skin, and something inside him gave way. He pulled her arms tight against his chest and crushed his face into her hands. And then, and there, for everything lost and everything stolen, both from him and by him in all these long years, the Godslayer started to sob.”</i><br /><br />I really wish those two would have gotten a chance to be happy, but as it seems the scars of their pasts ruined everything they could have been. Poor Azareen! To love her husband, to see his torture but to be unable to help him, to be incapable of saving him from the darkness that’s clutching at his tormented soul. It hurt to read about them and it hurt to see them so broken. No one in this story was truly bad; they all were just a product of the gods and what they did to them, so yeah. I felt sorry for Azareen and Eril-Fane, but that quote above gives me hope. Maybe they’ll manage to find each other in the next book? =) There’s always hope, right? <br /><br /><b>Conclusion:</b><br /><br />I loved this book!!! <b>“Strange the Dreamer”</b> was a wonderful and surprisingly awesome read and I can’t wait until “The Muse of Nightmares” is released! I need to know how it continues and what is going to happen next!!! I just need to know! XD<br /><br />So until the book is finally hitting the stores I’ll just try to hold on to this quote:<br /><br /><i>”And that’s how you go on. You lay laughter over the dark parts. The more dark parts, the more you have to laugh. With defiance, with abandon, with hysteria, any way you can.”</i><br /><br />Also a big thanks to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/69472742-rusty-grey" rel="nofollow noopener">The Awesome Rusty</a>!!! It was amazing to buddy read with you and I hope we’ll do this again! *lol* This truly was a buddy read match made in heaven because for some reason we always managed to be on the same page. Haha! I don’t know how we did this, but we must have some sort of superpower that linked us together and caused us to sync whenever it was needed. XD <br />Well, however we did it, it was certainly one of the most comfortable buddy reads I ever had the pleasure to experience. Rusty, you rock! ;-)</span>
  <a data-text-id="10600202674456233997" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily (Books with Emily Fox)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily (Books with Emily Fox)" href="/user/show/58160628-emily-books-with-emily-fox">Emily (Books with Emily Fox)</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer11882547907502365810">I liked the first half of the book. The world building was interesting, the magical powers of the children of the dead gods were interesting.... but then the second half was mostly a love story. A YA insta-love story... It ended up reducing my rating.<br/><br/>Overall I think this book is overhyped.</span>
