<div id="review_1509213018" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1509213018" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1509213018?book_show_action=true">Jan 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=why-yes-i-ya">why-yes-i-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1509213018" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15840261813602231372"><b>oooh, goodreads choice awards semifinalist for best YA fantasy! what will happen?</b><br/><br/>laini taylor is a straight-up godsend. she’s masterful at writing characters you care about, at building worlds down to the dust in the corner of a room, at creating conflicts that are analogous to a reader’s experiences despite being set in imaginary realms populated by creatures not-quite-human, and she’ll rip your heart out with zero regrets. <br/><br/>this book opens with the death of a character you’ve never met, so your</span>
  <span id="freeText15840261813602231372" style="display:none"><b>oooh, goodreads choice awards semifinalist for best YA fantasy! what will happen?</b><br><br>laini taylor is a straight-up godsend. she’s masterful at writing characters you care about, at building worlds down to the dust in the corner of a room, at creating conflicts that are analogous to a reader’s experiences despite being set in imaginary realms populated by creatures not-quite-human, and she’ll rip your heart out with zero regrets. <br><br>this book opens with the death of a character you’ve never met, so your heart stays right where it is, and then it schoomps back in time and you’re deep into a hundred or so pages following the story of a dreamy booknerd named lazlo strange (dreamy like “strange the dreamer,” not dreamy like [insert name of whatever celebrity is considered to be dreamy these days]) and his devotion to reading all the books, with an especial attraction to fairytales and stories about “the unseen city,” a land so far and mysterious that it has become the stuff of legend - warriors and creatures and magic, a city whose true name vanished from memory in an instant and is now known as weep. and this segment is all packed with details of war and lazlo’s obscure origins and his place within his world and magic and alchemy and unexpected opportunity and how books broke his nose and changed his life and by the time you meet up with the character whose death you witnessed in the prologue, you’re inundated with minutia and have half-forgotten that even happened. <br><br>but the other half remembers, and the more you get to know her, the more you don’t want to care too much about her as a character, because you know where this road ends. it’s no fun - braced for the inevitable thing that’s coming while the characters are themselves unaware, wanting there to be a creative loophole that will make things seem less …final.<br><br>it’s like how sean of the house came home when i was bingewatching OITNB season 5 and hung out for a bit and now that he’s joined me on my complete series rewatch, he’s already prepared for the death of a beloved someone that shocked us all when it happened, and now he’s in that uncomfortable position of knowing who but not when or how, and he’s not gonna feel the heartpunch as much as if he had just watched the show with me from the beginning, as i beseeched him to do. <br><br>seeing the future has never been something to envy, powerball aside. <br><br>overall, i didn’t love this as much as i loved the daughter of smoke and bone trilogy, which is still one of the best things i’ve ever read, particularly that middle book. there were times here when i thought her trademark poetical flourishes were strained and some of the banter was too cutesy, and it took a while to get going, but it’s still SO. DAMN. GOOD. <br><br>because she ended it with a friggin’ surgical strike to the feels.<br><br>just when you thought you were safe - when the thing you knew was gonna happen happened and you’re comforting yourself by googling silver linings and lemonade recipes for all these sour sour lemons, that’s when laini taylor swoops in and rips your heart out for real, and she’s all, “sucks to your lemonade, son!”<br><br>it’s like that line from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18770398.Night_Film" title="Night Film by Marisha Pessl" rel="nofollow noopener">Night Film</a>:<br><br><i>Just when you think you've hit rock bottom, you realize you're on another trapdoor.</i><br><br>i am so ready for the second part of this.<br><br><br>******************************************<br><br><i>the aftermath of a war between gods and men.<br>a mysterious city stripped of its name.<br>a mythic hero with blood on his hands.<br>a young librarian with a singular dream.<br>a girl every bit as dangerous as she is in danger.<br>alchemy and blood candy, nightmares and godspawn, moths and monsters, friendship and treachery, love and carnage.</i><br><br>on the one hand, that kind of sounds like drunk mad libs. <br><br>on the other hand, i LOVE drunk mad libs.<br><br>blood candy?? moths? carnage? librarian??<br><br>i want this like crazy.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15840261813602231372" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kiki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kiki" href="/user/show/4074594-kiki">Kiki</a>

                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1966510688&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1966510688" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1662349547686664209">I’m going to reread this. Which means new RTC. Also, this old review was just hot garbage. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2159311089" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2159311089" />
    <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey"><img alt="Chelsea Humphrey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585613513p2/47207032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2159311089?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea Humphrey" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey">Chelsea Humphrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2159311089" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7833291193203080095"><b>mahal</b>-<i>A risk that will yield either tremendous reward or disastrous consequence.</i><br/><br/>That's really the heart of what every reader desires in a fantasy world, right? Where there is no great risk, there is nothing worth losing, and where there is nothing worth losing, there is nothing worth reading. Perhaps that is the pinnacle of this book's excellence, but it's certainly not it's only great feature. I knew from the moment I dove in that this story would be special; the three pages of prologue were mo</span>
  <span id="freeText7833291193203080095" style="display:none"><b>mahal</b>-<i>A risk that will yield either tremendous reward or disastrous consequence.</i><br /><br />That's really the heart of what every reader desires in a fantasy world, right? Where there is no great risk, there is nothing worth losing, and where there is nothing worth losing, there is nothing worth reading. Perhaps that is the pinnacle of this book's excellence, but it's certainly not it's only great feature. I knew from the moment I dove in that this story would be special; the three pages of prologue were more beautiful, captivating, and gripping than the entirety of many books I've previously read. I could go on and on and on and on <s>and on and on and on and on</s> about the quality, structure, and exquisite nature of the writing, but I won't. I think it's been duly noted in most reviews that the dreamy state of writing creates an unparalleled atmosphere to enhance our experience within such a delicate fantasy world. I would liken it to <i>"calligraphy, if calligraphy were written in honey."</i><br /><br /><i>"Vengeance... Vengeance ought to be spoken through gritted teeth, spittle flying, the cords of one's soul so entangled in it that you can't let it go, even if you try."</i><br /><br /><b>THE PLOT</b><br />Best if you go into this knowing as little as possible, but for readers who need something to go on, there is a multi-layered plot that plays with the mind and the heart here. The beginning, after the prologue, is a slow building form of storytelling where we spend time getting to know Lazlo Strange and his part in this epic tale. Much emotion and feeling is infused here; I found this to be vital to the story as it forged my bond with Strange and welded my needs, hopes, and dreams with his own. Along the way, we are introduced to a new viewpoint where a similar form of storytelling is relayed. Once the two voices connect and intertwine, the pacing picks up and I really flew through to the end. While I would say this was easy to put down, I don't mean that in a negative way; this was simply a novel I wanted to savor and not rush through. I was able to completely immerse myself in this fantasy world and was thinking about it constantly throughout my day, but I felt comfortable doing this with no pressure to sneak around and cram in a few pages every spare second I had. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <i>"Sarai was the Muse of Nightmares"</i>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>THE CHARACTERS</b><br />We find out the above spoiler fairly early on, which I'm assuming pertains heavily to the next book as well, but I wanted to block it out for those who want no information. While there is quite a bit of action in the final 75 pages or so, the majority of the book is epic characterization and faultless world building. The atmosphere is simultaneously whimsical and bleak; it was equal parts bleary loss and gleaming hope. It felt strange and wonderful to be a part of something so unique as it truly contained a dreamlike, wispy quality, whereas most fantasy I've read does not contain this aesthetic. Even the scenes at the end featuring war, cruelty, and violence contained that lighter, more beautiful aesthetic. <s>Oh no! She's headed back to talking about the prose! Watch out!</s> Seriously, this writing is otherworldly. <br /><br /><i>"She didn't take away his conflicting emotions, although she could have. She left his hate there, right beside the love. It was the hate of the used and tormented, who are the children of the used and tormented... And it was love. Love that sets forth the soul like springtime and ripens it like summer. Love as rarely exists in reality..."</i><br /><br />I'll wrap this up, but I honestly was broken by that ending in the best possible way. If you haven't read the book, then pick it up immediately. It truly deserves all of the stars. If you have, then I'm sure we are all in agreement that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Sarai dying, while expected, was entirely emotional and heart wrenching, and also that Minya is a fabulous little nugget of a villain and those final chilling words have me begging for Laini to write as fast as she can because I NEED <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25446343.Muse_of_Nightmares__Strange_the_Dreamer___2_" title="Muse of Nightmares (Strange the Dreamer, #2) by Laini Taylor" rel="nofollow noopener">The Muse of Nightmares</a>!!!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Some of the finest writing I have had the pleasure of experiencing all year and easily my favorite fantasy to date, I highly recommend you read this. &lt;3<br /><br /><i>*Thanks Bentley for buddy reading this one with me! </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="7833291193203080095" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11068518787252811045" style="display:none"><b>YES! PRINTZ HONOR!!!</b><br /><br /><br />You are in for a treat. <br /><br />I mean, if you are a Laini Taylor fan and like her elaborate prose and rich worldbuilding and, let's be frank, romances with a whiff of instalove, I don't see how this book can disappoint you. It surely didn't disappoint me.<br /><br />The story starts with a hungry orphan dreaming of a magic city beyond a vast desert where all kinds of wonders live. And ends... Well, I'll stop here because the biggest pleasure in reading Taylor's books is unspooling a wondrous yarn of her storytelling.<br /><br />But rest assured, there are gods and wars with both sides guilty of unspeakable, "inter-species" love, guilt and envy, shame and regret, and impossible choices - all themes not unfamiliar to fans of Daughter of Smoke and Bone. And yet this story is also unique and irresistibly captivating.</span>

<div id="review_1955179832" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1955179832" />
    <a title="Hannah Greendale" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43377498-hannah-greendale"><img alt="Hannah Greendale" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466436186p2/43377498.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1955179832?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah Greendale" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah Greendale" href="/user/show/43377498-hannah-greendale">Hannah Greendale</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43377498-hannah-greendale?shelf=printz-award-nominee">printz-award-nominee</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1955179832" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15839387420586169390"><a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=f34XzCtirjg' rel='nofollow noopener'>Click here</a> to watch a video review of this book on my channel, <i>From Beginning to Bookend</i>.<br/><br/><a href='https://imgur.com/6kLHT7y' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1515604004i/24865327._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Lazlo Strange, abandoned orphan and bibliophile librarian, has nurtured an interest in fairy tales and legends since he was a boy. His secret passion is studying the language and lore of the lost city of Weep. Lazlo believes he'll never be brave enough to search for the forgotten city, but when a heroic figure known as the Godslayer arrives at his village in search of aid, the opportunity to cross the wo</span>
  <span id="freeText15839387420586169390" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=f34XzCtirjg" rel="nofollow noopener">Click here</a> to watch a video review of this book on my channel, <i>From Beginning to Bookend</i>.<br><br><a href="https://imgur.com/6kLHT7y" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1515604004i/24865327._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Lazlo Strange, abandoned orphan and bibliophile librarian, has nurtured an interest in fairy tales and legends since he was a boy. His secret passion is studying the language and lore of the lost city of Weep. Lazlo believes he'll never be brave enough to search for the forgotten city, but when a heroic figure known as the Godslayer arrives at his village in search of aid, the opportunity to cross the world is suddenly within his grasp. <br><br><i>Strange the Dreamer</i> offers the same luscious and imaginative prose one can always anticipate from a novel written by Laini Taylor. <br><br><i> The black trees danced. His breath-ghost scudded away on a gust, only to be replaced by another. His shadow played out huge before him, and his mind gleamed with ancient wars and winged beings, a mountain of melted demon bones and the city on the far side of it - a city that had vanished in the mists of time.</i> <br><br><i>One [dress] had a skirt like a cage carved of whalebone, another a long train made of hundreds of doves' wings all stitched together. There was a bodice of pure molded gold, made to look like a beetle's carapace, and a fan collar fashioned from the spines of poisonous fish, with tiny teeth sewn in patterns like seed pearls. There were headdresses and veils, corsets with daggers concealed in the stays, elaborate capes, and teetering tall shoes carved of ebony and coral.</i> <br><br>There's a considerable amount of foundational exposition and world building, as this is the first book in a new series, but the author finds a delicate balance between introducing readers to a new world with never-before-seen mythical creatures and delivering a complete story with a cast of intriguing characters. While Lazlo makes for a likable and refreshing protagonist, he's accompanied by a batch of equally alluring characters such as a tricky alchemist, a sage monk, a sly thief, and a blue-skinned goddess, to name a few. <br><br>This book is a mixed bag of everything readers want from an epic fantasy: magic and whimsy; a fresh take on supernatural abilities; a compelling mystery; an undeniable sense of exploration and adventure; a new realm of fantastical proportions, and a satisfying ending that sets the stage for more to come. <br><br>Locales are easy to visualize in one's mind, character motivations sing with truth, and the electric thrill of young love is portrayed with velvet language: <br><br><i>There was a dusting of nearly invisible freckles on the bridge of her nose. The glide of their faces was as slow as poured honey, and</i> her lips<i>. Ever so slightly, they parted. The bottom one, voluptuous as dew-bright fruit, parted from its fellow -</i> for him<i> - and it was the most enticing thing he'd ever seen. A blaze of desire surged through him and he leaned into the honey-slowness, pushing the hopelessness out of his way to take that sweet, soft lip between his own.</i> <br><br>A dazzling start to an exhilarating new series, <i>Strange the Dreamer</i> offers beauty and wonder, magic and mysticism, monsters and gods.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15839387420586169390" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1722115657" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1722115657" />
    <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz"><img alt="Helena of Eretz ✰" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596076376p2/27036454.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1722115657?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helena of Eretz ✰" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz">Helena of Eretz ✰</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=hardback">hardback</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=signed">signed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=best-of-2017">best-of-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1722115657" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8892940622453633865"><i>Re-read with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1860903011' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lynn</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2265102153' rel='nofollow noopener'>Alison</a></i> ... I shall turn you into Laini Taylor-addicts like me in no time! <b>MUAHAHAHA</b>! ;)<br/><br/>A <b>new Laini Taylor book</b>, you say? Don’t mind if I do… <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1552780823ra/27216209.gif' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Perhaps you’d like some footage of me, when I <i>accidentally</i> found <b>an autographed copy</b> of my favourite author’s new book:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1552780823ra/27216215.gif' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Let’s just start off by taking a moment to appreciate the fact that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28449207.Strange_the_Dreamer__Strange_the_Dreamer___1_' title='Strange the Dreamer (Strange the Dreamer, #1) by Laini Taylor' rel='nofollow noopener'>Strange the Dreamer</a> was selected as a <b>Michael L. Printz honour book</b> (the silver sticker on the cover). All I can say is that it is extremely well-dese</span>
  <span id="freeText8892940622453633865" style="display:none"><i>Re-read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1860903011" rel="nofollow noopener">Lynn</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2265102153" rel="nofollow noopener">Alison</a></i> ... I shall turn you into Laini Taylor-addicts like me in no time! <b>MUAHAHAHA</b>! ;)<br><br>A <b>new Laini Taylor book</b>, you say? Don’t mind if I do… <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1552780823ra/27216209.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Perhaps you’d like some footage of me, when I <i>accidentally</i> found <b>an autographed copy</b> of my favourite author’s new book:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1552780823ra/27216215.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Let’s just start off by taking a moment to appreciate the fact that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28449207.Strange_the_Dreamer__Strange_the_Dreamer___1_" title="Strange the Dreamer (Strange the Dreamer, #1) by Laini Taylor" rel="nofollow noopener">Strange the Dreamer</a> was selected as a <b>Michael L. Printz honour book</b> (the silver sticker on the cover). All I can say is that it is extremely well-deserved because this book is a <i>MASTERPIECE</i>. Laini stayed true to the <b>lovely and lush writing style</b> that I fell in love with all those years ago. <br><br><i>WOW. MY GOD.</i> I didn’t think it was possible, but this might have just chucked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8490112.Daughter_of_Smoke___Bone__Daughter_of_Smoke___Bone___1_" title="Daughter of Smoke &amp; Bone (Daughter of Smoke &amp; Bone, #1) by Laini Taylor" rel="nofollow noopener">Daughter of Smoke &amp; Bone</a> to the side as my <b>favourite series of all time</b>. In Queen Laini’s usual <b>style of brilliance</b>, I was glued to my seat while reading this and would’ve finished it <i>A LOT</i> sooner if uni didn’t exist. <br><br><i>What did I love about it, you ask?</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1552780823ra/27216207.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>“‘You’re a storyteller. Dream up something wild and improbable,’ she pleaded. ‘Something beautiful and full of monsters.’<br>‘Beautiful and full of monsters?’<br>‘All the best stories are.’”</i><br><br>This is a <i>faery tale</i>. This is tale of <i>mythology</i>. This is a <i>love story</i>. This is story of <i>gods and heroes</i>. This is <i>beautiful and full of monsters</i> (wink, wink). This is a book of…<i>everything</i>.<br><br>I don’t want to <i>accidentally</i> spoil anyone, and nor do I know how to discuss this without <b>spoilers</b>, so I’m going to provide a general…<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1552780823ra/27216210.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>THIS IS YOUR LAST WARNING!!!</i><br><br><b>Fine. It’s your funeral.</b> :P<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552780823i/27216211._SY540_.png" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552780823i/27216219._SY540_.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>“He read while he walked. He read while he ate. The other librarians suspected he somehow read while he slept, or perhaps didn't sleep at all.”</i><br><br>Our story begins with the little <b>cinnamon roll</b> that is <b>Lazlo Strange</b>. He’s a precious little <b>war-orphan</b> who’s actually 20 years of age, but is so bloody cute. He is definitely <i>more mature and sophisticated</i> than a typical YA protagonist, and nor does he make <i>ridiculously stupid decisions</i>, which was refreshing. He is a <b>Junior Librarian</b>, aka the male version of <i>MOI</i>. By that, I mean he <i>LOVES</i> books, walks into walls while reading, and had his nose broken by the “villain” book of faery tales that fell down on his face on his <i>FIRST DAY</i>. He’s just too <b>sweet and adorable</b> for words. He <b>helps people</b> for no reason other than the fact that they are in need of help, never asking for the favour to be returned or payment for his services. <br><br><i>“Without his books, his room felt like a body with its hearts cut out.”</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552780823i/27216208._SX540_.png" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>“It was impossible, of course. But when did that ever stop any dreamer from dreaming.”</i><br><br>Lazlo was raised by uncompromising <b>monks</b>, but only the senile one would tell him stories. Most of those stories were about <b>a city</b>, far beyond the desert, now <b>lost to the world</b>, including Zosma, which is where they currently are. But one day, the name of the city was erased from everyone’s memories and replaced with the word, “<b>Weep</b>.”<br><br>Ultimately, we learn that Weep was cut off from the world because of the arrival of <b>six blue-skinned gods</b>. <b>Skathis</b> was the god of beasts and lord of the <b>mesarthium</b> (an impenetrable metal). <b>Isagol</b> was the goddess of despair. <b>Vanth</b> was the god of storms. <b>Korako</b> was the goddess of secrets. <b>Ikirok</b> was the god of revelry. <b>Letha</b> was the goddess of oblivion. For <i>two hundred years</i>, the gods inhabited the floating <b>Citadel</b> in the sky, made of mesarthium. Over and over again, the gods would <b>abduct the young men and women</b> of Weep in order to <b>breed thousands of godspawn</b>, each with magical gifts of their own. After a few years, the men and women were returned to the city below, with <i>no memories of what occurred to them</i> in the Citadel. The godspawn, on the other hand, were never seen again, after their magical gifts manifested in the nursery. Thousands of children went <i>POOF</i>. <br><br><i>“You think good people can't hate?" she asked. "You think good people don't kill? ... Good people do all the things bad people do, Lazlo. It's just that when they do them, they call it justice.”</i><br><br><b>Eril-Fane, the Godslayer</b>, married the love of his life, <b>Azareen</b>, <i>five days</i> before he was abducted by the gods. For <i>three years</i>, he was forced to serve as Isagol’s consort, where he <b>inherently hated her</b> and was <b>compelled to love her</b> simultaneously. Their time together ultimately resulted in the <b>birth of Sarai</b>. When Azareen was <i>abducted and raped</i>, Eril-Fane’s love for his wife overpowered the compulsion that Isagol had over him. He then <b>slaughtered the six gods and the thirty godspawn</b> in the nursery. The abducted humans, including Eril-Fane and Azareen, left the Citadel with their memories intact, having killed Letha before she could erase them. However, she spitefully had her revenge by <i>erasing the memory of the city’s name</i> from the world, replacing it with “<b>Weep</b>.”<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552780823i/27216212._SY540_.png" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>“And that's how you go on. You lay laughter over the dark parts. The more dark parts, the more you have to laugh. With defiance, with abandon, with hysteria, any way you can.”</i><br><br>The <b>eldest of the godspawn</b> in the nursery was a six-year old, <b>Minya</b>, who escaped what is referred to as Eril-Fane’s “<b>Carnage</b>.” Her magical gift is being able to <b>capture and control ghosts</b>. She caught enough of them to create an <i>army of the undead</i> in the Citadel, but used a few of them to help raise the babies. Somehow, Minya <b>never aged</b> after all this time, retaining the appearance of a six-year old. During the Carnage, she managed to <b>carry four babies</b> with her into hiding. They were:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552780823i/27216220._SX540_.png" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552780823i/27216218._SY540_.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Sarai, the “Muse of Nightmares</b>,” screamed and channelled her consciousness into a hundred moths. These moths could then lay upon the brows of dreamers, allowing her see and <b>control their dreams</b>, even turning them into nightmares. She’s the only one who could see what went on in the city below them.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552780823i/27216216._SY540_.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Feral, the “Cloud Thief</b>,” stole clouds from faraway. He could call rain clouds, snow, hail, and even lightning to the Citadel. He was their <b>sole source of water</b>, which kept them alive.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552780823i/27216221._SY540_.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Sparrow, the “Orchid Witch</b>,” made plants grow or wilt. Her ability to <b>make the Kimril plant flourish</b> was fundamental to their survival, as well, because Kimril was a flavourless vegetable with enough nutrients to keep them alive.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552780823i/27216217._SY540_.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Ruby, the “Bonfire</b>,” could <b>combust into flames</b>, creating warmth in the Citadel.<br><br>We then learn that Eril-Fane wants to <b>remove the Citadel</b> from Weep’s sky, thus threatening the <i>secret lives that the godspawn have led</i> until now. He <b>led a convoy</b> to foreign nations, including Zosma, in search of the <i>keenest intelligence and the extraordinarily skilled</i> to <b>address Weep’s problem</b>. In exchange for their help, he promises <b>unimaginable treasure</b> to the one who solves it. The convoy eventually includes:<br><br><b>Ebliz Todd, the builder</b>, most notable for building the Cloudspire, the tallest structure in the world.<br><br><b>Calixte Dagaz, the acrobat</b>, who climbed the 600-foot Cloudspire with only her hands and bare feet because she wanted to raid the tomb inside.<br><br><b>Thyon Nero, the alchemist</b> and Prince of Zosma, who distilled azoth, the medium for making gold.<br><br><b>Jonwit Belabra, the mathematician</b>.<br><br><b>Phathmus Mouzaive, the natural philosopher</b>, who focused in magnetic fields.<br><br><b>Kae Ilfurth, the engineer</b>.<br><br><b>The Fellerings, the metallurgists</b>, who were a set of twins.<br><br><b>Fortune Kether, the artist</b>, most renowned for his frescoes in public and his catapults and siege machines in private.<br><br><b>Drave, the explosionist</b>, known for setting charges in mines and blowing the sides off of mountains.<br><br><b>Soulzeren Eoh, the farmer-botanist, and Ozwin Eoh, the mechanist</b>. Together, they invented a <i>silk sleigh, a craft that could fly</i>.<br><br><i>“He wasn't an alchemist, or a hero. He was a librarian, and a dreamer. He was a reader, and the unsung expert on a long-lost city no one cared a thing about.”</i><br><br>And finally, Eril-Fane agrees to bring <b>Lazlo</b> along, as well. He basically volunteers to be <b>Eril-Fane’s secretary</b> and to be the <b>errand-boy for the convoy</b>, just for the <i>opportunity</i> to go to Weep. Lazlo’s studies of Weep (even uncovering the alphabet and recreating the language) were <b>his life’s work</b> and he wanted to finally see it for himself. The monks, librarians, and scholars <i>all forgot and dismissed Weep</i> as a fictional place, but Lazlo never did. He <b>unconditionally always loved it</b> and believed in it.<br><br>Once we reach this point in the novel, it goes <b>full-speed ahead</b>, all the way until the end. Get ready for the ride of your lives!!! I didn’t guess a <i>SINGLE PLOT POINT</i> in this entire novel (except for Lazlo turning out to be one of the godspawn).<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552780823i/27216224._SX540_.png" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552780823i/27216226._SY540_.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>“I think you’re a fairy tale. I think you’re magical, and brave, and exquisite. And I hope you'll let me be in your story.”</i><br><br>I’m not even going to lie…my favourite part of the book was <b>Dream Weep</b>. What a <b>pure and magical place</b> that I’m <i>SO MAD</i> that I’ll never get to see it <i>IN REAL LIFE</i> with my own two eyes! <i>UGH!</i> And it just sounds like my ideal world, too. I mean, there’s a centaur and his lady on a date. <i>HOW COOL IS THAT?!!!</i> He bought dragon wings for himself and fox wings for Sarai at the wingsmith shop with dream money! Speaking of him and Sarai…<i>AGH!</i> Lazlo is <b>so sweet and romantic and pure</b>! Can I have a man who woos me like Lazlo? For crying out loud, he bought Sarai a bracelet with every phase of the moon for her because the moon was stolen from her! How utterly cute!!! He even planned out a lakeside (or was it seaside?) tea party, where he had the teapot pour for itself because he feared that he’d spill it from nerves. <b>Oh. My. Gosh.</b> I just can’t with his sweetness. He also imagined dream cakes for the tea party!!! And when he found out about Sarai’s nightmares…what was his response? <i>“Turn [nightmares] into fireflies and catch them in jars.”</i> <i>SOMEONE PROTECT SARAI AND LAZLO AT ALL COSTS!</i> They deserve <b>cakes and hugs and kisses and all the happiness in the world</b>! What sweet and pure protagonists. &lt;3<br><br>And yes, as Laini Taylor tends to do, there is a bit of <b>instalove</b> in this. <i>BUT IT WORKS</i>. By the time it occurs, we've spent so much time with Sarai and Lazlo individually that we've fallen in love with them already. In Lazlo's dreams, they've spent <b>so many scenes together</b> in both <i>silliness and seriousness, happiness and sadness</i> that I didn't mind watching them <b>fall in love</b> with each other in <b>a short amount of time</b>. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552780823i/27216213._SX540_.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And, although Laini Taylor <b>did tell us</b> what was going to occur from the beginning…<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552780823i/27216225._SY540_.png" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552780823i/27216214._SY540_.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>“The mahalath had come and remade them both. He was a god, and she was a ghost. A page had turned. A new story was beginning. You had only to look at Lazlo to know it would be brilliant. And Sarai could not be in it.”</i><br><br><i>SHE STILL BROKE MY HEART!!! WHY, LAINI?!!! WHYYY?!!!</i> Why did <b>Sarai</b> have to be the one who <b>fell from the Citadel</b>???<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1552780823ra/27216222.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I can’t handle <b>all of these emotions</b> and need to mend my broken heart <i>ASAP</i>. So, in conclusion, I have only one thing left to say, and that is…<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1552780823ra/27216223.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="8892940622453633865" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1954802305" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1954802305" />
    <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes"><img alt="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598297811p2/1452829.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1954802305?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~" href="/user/show/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes">Mary ~Ravager of Tomes~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=owned-physical">owned-physical</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1954802305" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15680843032456839602"><b>***11/19/2017 GET IT <a href='https://mobile.audible.com/pd/Teens/Strange-the-Dreamer-Audiobook/B01NBW5LNR?ref=a_home-page_c11_dd&pf_rd_p=71ba1fb1-ed3d-4a18-a8ed-a980cfd175d0&pf_rd_r=RX9YEDVF6DPHKHXGDWTX&' rel='nofollow noopener'>HERE</a> ON AUDIBLE DAILY DEAL $5.95 That is a freakin' steal oh my god***</b><br/><br/><b>Peculiar. Resplendent. Gripping.</b><br/><br/>These are just a couple of words that race through my mind when I consider <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28449207.Strange_the_Dreamer__Strange_the_Dreamer___1_' title='Strange the Dreamer (Strange the Dreamer, #1) by Laini Taylor' rel='nofollow noopener'>Strange the Dreamer</a>. <br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/324620.Laini_Taylor' title='Laini Taylor' rel='nofollow noopener'>Laini Taylor</a> has solidified her spot as one of my <u>favorite</u> authors with this release. <br/><br/>I am <b>unapologetically</b> in love with her style of writing. I am a <b>shameless worshiper</b> of her artistry for willing forth magnificent worlds & characters & scenarios from her pen. <br/><br/><b>I devour her books </b></span>
  <span id="freeText15680843032456839602" style="display:none"><b>***11/19/2017 GET IT <a href="https://mobile.audible.com/pd/Teens/Strange-the-Dreamer-Audiobook/B01NBW5LNR?ref=a_home-page_c11_dd&amp;pf_rd_p=71ba1fb1-ed3d-4a18-a8ed-a980cfd175d0&amp;pf_rd_r=RX9YEDVF6DPHKHXGDWTX&amp;" rel="nofollow noopener">HERE</a> ON AUDIBLE DAILY DEAL $5.95 That is a freakin' steal oh my god***</b><br /><br /><b>Peculiar. Resplendent. Gripping.</b><br /><br />These are just a couple of words that race through my mind when I consider <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28449207.Strange_the_Dreamer__Strange_the_Dreamer___1_" title="Strange the Dreamer (Strange the Dreamer, #1) by Laini Taylor" rel="nofollow noopener">Strange the Dreamer</a>. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/324620.Laini_Taylor" title="Laini Taylor" rel="nofollow noopener">Laini Taylor</a> has solidified her spot as one of my <u>favorite</u> authors with this release. <br /><br />I am <b>unapologetically</b> in love with her style of writing. I am a <b>shameless worshiper</b> of her artistry for willing forth magnificent worlds &amp; characters &amp; scenarios from her pen. <br /><br /><b>I devour her books like oxygen.</b><br /><br />Before I get ahead of myself, I want to mention that I <i>did</i> notice some small things that bothered me here and there, which I will detail later. <br /><br />However, I still chose to give this book a 5 stars because <u>overall I don't feel those issues weigh enough to affect my rating.</u><br /><br /><b>This is one of the richest worlds we have seen from Taylor yet.</b><br /><br />We focus mostly on the city of Weep, but the story is crafted in such a way that it suggests magnitude beyond that focus. It's crafted from a bloody, fantastical history. It's <b>teeming</b> with science &amp; lore &amp; magic.<br /><br /><b>This is the type of world I savor.</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>"Beautiful, and full of monsters."</i>
</b><br /><br />I appreciate the intense degree of characterization in this novel. I got such a well-formed picture for each character in my mind while I read, especially our two main characters, Lazlo and Sarai.<br /><br />Lazlo is a tender-hearted librarian, and entirely consumed by his whimsical imagination. His dreams and benevolence run as deep as the ocean, <i>and I tripped and fell head over heels for him almost immediately.</i><br /><br /><b>Strange the Dreamer.</b><br /><br />Sarai is a solemn, intelligent godspawn. She is woven from the material of conflict, light and darkness spun into the form of a young woman. She is at war with her own compassion, experiencing both hatred &amp; empathy for the opposing sides of a war she almost didn't survive.<br /><br /><b>The Muse of Nightmares.</b><br /><br /><u>I believed in both of these characters.</u> I was never bored with either perspective. I was ravaging my fingernails while waiting to see how this dreadfully exquisite plot would unravel. <br /><br /><b>This story is much more than the sum of its parts.</b><br /><br />It's about the ferocity of love &amp; hope. It's about the persistence of hatred &amp; prejudice. It's about underestimating people, and overestimating people, and finding out whether or not we are capable of forgiveness.<br /><br />As for my issues, of course we do see a small bit of insta-love. <b>It was not a glaring problem.</b> Taylor's style of writing and depth of characterization almost always keep my suspension of disbelief intact. <br /><br />Reading the about Lazlo and Sarai gave me that giddy, fresh love, honeymoon infatuation feeling you get when you first begin seeing someone. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>Your heart flutters &amp; your breath hitches and the pure potential for a spectacular love leaves you glowing.</i>
</b><br /><br />And so just like with the <i>Daughter of Smoke and Bone</i> series, I found it easy to excuse any insta-love hints I may have seen.<br /><br />Also, the pacing for the first 70% of the book was <u>rather slow</u> but if you know anything about me, <b>I'm almost never bothered by a slow pace.</b><br /><br />I actually prefer it because I feel it gives the author a chance to properly introduce and provide adequate details for the story they're writing. <br /><br />Objectively though, I can see where some may feel it was <b>too slow.</b><br /><br />But this book was <u>
  <b>everything</b>
</u> for me. Laini Taylor is the kind of artist who inspires me to want to create and add something beautiful to this world.<br /><br /><b>I adore this book &amp; I want nothing more than to get my hands on the next one.</b><br /><br /><i>This and other reviews of mine can be found on <a href="http://booknest.eu/reviews/34-mary-s-reviews/426-strangethedreamer" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Nest</a>!</i><br /><br />Buddy read this with my bad-boy lovin' bff <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/14717996-kainat-ijaz-unpopular-opinion-alert" rel="nofollow noopener">Kainat</a> &amp; the terrifying but tremendous <b>dark</b> lord herself <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/35147071-jenn-the-crimson-dark-lord-scribe-house-of-slytheread" rel="nofollow noopener">Jennymort!</a> And basically the rest of Goodreads, who are we kidding.</span>

<div id="review_2783872142" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2783872142" />
    <a title="Mark Lawrence" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4508542-mark-lawrence"><img alt="Mark Lawrence" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442536170p2/4508542.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2783872142?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mark Lawrence" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mark Lawrence" href="/user/show/4508542-mark-lawrence">Mark Lawrence</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2783872142" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7063007063998133905">"That was the year Zosma sank to its knees and bled great gouts of men into a war about nothing." <br/><br/>This is a very well written book. Laini Taylor writes beautiful prose.<br/><br/>It's also very imaginative, there are ideas in it that really impressed me. It's a book that's low on violence and action - high in character, mystery, and especially ... beauty. <br/><br/>The first big chunk of the book is spent with our hero, the eponymous Strange, most of it in a library - a surprisingly common location for fantasy stori</span>
  <span id="freeText7063007063998133905" style="display:none">"That was the year Zosma sank to its knees and bled great gouts of men into a war about nothing." <br /><br />This is a very well written book. Laini Taylor writes beautiful prose.<br /><br />It's also very imaginative, there are ideas in it that really impressed me. It's a book that's low on violence and action - high in character, mystery, and especially ... beauty. <br /><br />The first big chunk of the book is spent with our hero, the eponymous Strange, most of it in a library - a surprisingly common location for fantasy stories. I guess Name of the Wind has the most famous library in fantasy but vast and ancient libraries are very nicely presented in many other tales such as Wolfe's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/60211.The_Shadow_of_the_Torturer__The_Book_of_the_New_Sun___1_" title="The Shadow of the Torturer (The Book of the New Sun, #1) by Gene Wolfe" rel="nofollow noopener">The Shadow of the Torturer</a> or Bancroft's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/35959733.Arm_of_the_Sphinx__The_Books_of_Babel___2_" title="Arm of the Sphinx (The Books of Babel, #2) by Josiah Bancroft" rel="nofollow noopener">Arm of the Sphinx</a>. Laslo is nicely developed as a thoroughly nice guy with an open mind, bags of curiosity, and an obsession with a "lost" city.<br /><br />Later on we're introduced to a group who represent another common device in fantasy - a family with diverse magical powers, much like the ones found in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26892110.The_Library_at_Mount_Char" title="The Library at Mount Char by Scott Hawkins" rel="nofollow noopener">The Library at Mount Char</a>, or Umbrella Academy, or even X-Men. But this doesn't mean it's unoriginal - the characters are wonderfully drawn and some of their powers are very interesting.<br /><br />Inevitably the two threads entwine and Laslo gets to interact with our family of godlings. A romance springs up but in a very charming way and a series of unusual settings. "Romance" can turn off as many readers as it attracts. In some it will evoke thoughts of heaving bodices in pulpy (but wildly popular novels) churned out in vast numbers. This is not that. What makes the romance at the heart of this book appealing to me is firstly that before it starts I have become invested individually in both participants, and secondly that it builds through witty, clever, touching, and insightful dialogue (banter even). <br /><br />It's a magical, mysterious, whimsical book with a hard edge to it. There is threat, loss, a dark history, and the fear that things will fall apart again.<br /><br />My only disappointment with the book is the ending (which felt rather rushed to me - although when I occasionally see someone say that about one or other my own books I snort and disagree :D ). The book ends on a cliffhanger. I would rather have seen it take a little more time, go in a somewhat different direction and have been a standalone. As a standalone with a more upbeat resolution I think it would have been a truly excellent book. As book 1 of a trilogy it is still a very fine read. I'm not sure where the next book will go and I'm in no particular rush to find out BUT I really enjoyed this read and strongly recommend you checking it out too.<br /><br /><br /> <a href="http://eepurl.com/cimnK1" rel="nofollow noopener">Join my 3-emails-a-year newsletter #prizes</a><br /><br /><br />....</span>
  <a data-text-id="7063007063998133905" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2482704482" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2482704482" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2482704482?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=forbidden-love">forbidden-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=war-setting">war-setting</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2482704482" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12507683655300284342">Can we all just agree that Laini Taylor is a goddess?<br/><br/>Not the kind of goddess who brings despair to your spirit, but the kind who appeases it with angelic words. <br/><br/>If you remember, this book’s publication date was postponed. It was released in March of 2017, but was supposed to hit the shelves months before.<br/><br/>I, like many others, was heartbroken when I got the news. I was even annoyed. How dare Laini Taylor do this to us? How dare she tease us in such a way?<br/><br/>Well. I can say, from the bottom of my hear</span>
  <span id="freeText12507683655300284342" style="display:none">Can we all just agree that Laini Taylor is a goddess?<br /><br />Not the kind of goddess who brings despair to your spirit, but the kind who appeases it with angelic words. <br /><br />If you remember, this book’s publication date was postponed. It was released in March of 2017, but was supposed to hit the shelves months before.<br /><br />I, like many others, was heartbroken when I got the news. I was even annoyed. How dare Laini Taylor do this to us? How dare she tease us in such a way?<br /><br />Well. I can say, from the bottom of my heart, that all is forgiven. If the story had been tremendously bad, I could have held a grudge maybe, but it’s not. It’s tremendously original, well-written, magical and romantic.<br /><br />There is everything you could possibly want from a fantasy tale: a carefully-constructed world-building with its own history and culture, developed characters—villains, heroes, and those in-between—, lush descriptions that speak of Laini Taylor’s way with words and passionate mind, as well as a forbidden love story that will be the focus of your dreams tonight. <br /><br />What is it about forbidden love that awakens my soul? Is it the secrecy of it? Or is it the intensity of the emotions of the two beings feeling them? Or the fact that it seems as though the whole world is against you, and yet you need no one but the person next to you? <br /><br />Yes, I am turning to mush. Please don’t step on me. I am at my most vulnerable state.<br /><br />There’s nothing else I want more right now than to plunge into the sequel. Nothing else. Who cares if one of my most anticipated 2018 books just came out? Not I. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12507683655300284342" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1930307468" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1930307468" />
    <a title="Charlotte May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14002983-charlotte-may"><img alt="Charlotte May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596906925p2/14002983.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1930307468?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Charlotte May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Charlotte May" href="/user/show/14002983-charlotte-may">Charlotte May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781444788945" href="/book/show/36187690-strange-the-dreamer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=500-page-plus">500-page-plus</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14002983-charlotte-may?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1930307468" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5580429467472411141"><i> “He read while he walked. He read while he ate. The other librarians suspected he somehow read while he slept, or perhaps didn’t sleep at all. On the occasions that he did look up from the page, he would seem as though he were awakening from a dream. ‘Strange the dreamer’ they called him. ‘That dreamer Strange.” </i> <br/><br/>Ok, so I think I fell into the trap of overhype with this one. Laini Taylor and I have an uncertain relationship. Her imagination cannot be faulted, the worlds she creates are truly re</span>
  <span id="freeText5580429467472411141" style="display:none"><i> “He read while he walked. He read while he ate. The other librarians suspected he somehow read while he slept, or perhaps didn’t sleep at all. On the occasions that he did look up from the page, he would seem as though he were awakening from a dream. ‘Strange the dreamer’ they called him. ‘That dreamer Strange.” </i> <br /><br />Ok, so I think I fell into the trap of overhype with this one. Laini Taylor and I have an uncertain relationship. Her imagination cannot be faulted, the worlds she creates are truly remarkable. But on the flip side she is heavily romanced focussed – way too much for me, which I discovered during her Daughter of Smoke and Bone trilogy. I also never really got the term ‘purple prose’ until I read her books – there’s in depth description, and then there’s an entire chapter on 2 people kissing…And Laini Taylor dives straight over the line and into the insta love. <br /><br />Strange the Dreamer has so many 5 star reviews, and when I read the synopsis I felt sure I’d love it. (I mean, I obviously enjoyed it by my 4 stars, but it didn’t make my favourites shelf, just to put it in perspective.) There was loads I loved, but there was quite a bit that hindered my reading experience. <br /><br />So, Lazlo Strange is an orphan, raised by monks until he gets the chance to work in the Great Library and become a librarian. From there he reads everything he possibly can, most specifically, any book on the mysterious city of Weep, a land that has had its name stolen; a land whose mysteries Lazlo is desperate to unravel.<br /><br />When a group of visitors from Weep arrive and invite a collection of the smartest and most innovative individuals to travel back with them, Lazlo knows this is his chance to discover his dream once and for all. He convinces their leader to take him with them, much to everyone else’s surprise, in particular Thyon Nero with whom Lazlo has a turbulent relationship.<br /><br />On arrival in Weep they discover a dark and violent history and a floating Citadel high above the city that the residents are unable to bring down or remove – hence the group of geniuses they’ve selected.<br /><br /><i> “We are all children in the dark, here in Weep.” </i><br /><br />Pros and Cons time, because I feel like making a list.<br /><br /><b>Pros</b><br />Lazlo Strange – his character is wonderful. He is bookish and curious and full of wonder. Loved him.<br />World building. The history of Weep was great, absolutely fascinating and cleverly built.<br />Minya’s character. She was creepy as fuck, but INTERESTING.<br />Sparrow – I love her with my whole heart.<br />Thyon was a great character to dislike – I was on the bandwagon for that.<br /><br /><b>Cons</b><br />Ruby and Feral (I won’t say what because spoilers. But just no to both of them)<br />Waaaaaaaay too much mushy stuff with Sarai and Lazlo. Like you could all die, want to hold off on making out for like five minutes?? Honestly. <br /><br /><i> “Beautiful and full of monsters? All the best stories are.” </i><br /><br />Overall I think I’m leaning more toward 3.5 and I’m slightly worried all the mega fans are gonna come after me, but please, leave it out.<br /><br /><br />*********************<br /><br />I have heard NOTHING but good things about this book, so come at me hype!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5580429467472411141" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1959064837" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1959064837" />
    <a title="Candace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16384209-candace"><img alt="Candace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459720769p2/16384209.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1959064837?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candace" href="/user/show/16384209-candace">Candace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28145767-strange-the-dreamer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=listened-to-audio-version">listened-to-audio-version</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=dangerous-hero-themed-books-read">dangerous-hero-themed-books-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=forbidden-romance">forbidden-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=revenge-stories">revenge-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=sweet-heart-warming-stories">sweet-heart-warming-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=shocking-twists">shocking-twists</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1959064837" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1230755875123001021">What a spectacular world Laini Taylor has crafted in this book! Every once in awhile I enjoy a paranormal/fantasy type of story, but it definitely isn't my go-to genre. Yet, Laini Taylor has managed to suck me in once again. The beauty of her words and the vivid imagery that she creates never ceases to amaze me. <br/><br/>This book centers on Lazlo Strange, aka "Strange the Dreamer". An orphan, he has never really had a home or felt like he fit in. The closest he's come to a sense of normalcy is during hi</span>
  <span id="freeText1230755875123001021" style="display:none">What a spectacular world Laini Taylor has crafted in this book! Every once in awhile I enjoy a paranormal/fantasy type of story, but it definitely isn't my go-to genre. Yet, Laini Taylor has managed to suck me in once again. The beauty of her words and the vivid imagery that she creates never ceases to amaze me. <br /><br />This book centers on Lazlo Strange, aka "Strange the Dreamer". An orphan, he has never really had a home or felt like he fit in. The closest he's come to a sense of normalcy is during his time in the Great Library. He grows up to become a librarian, submersing himself in the stories that he loves so much.<br /><br />More than anything else, he is captivated by tales of the "unseen city". He remembers hearing the stories about the city and the travelers that used to return from having crossed over the city's borders. Then one day, the city seemed to be forgotten. Unlike everyone else in his town, Lazlo remembers the feeling of having his memory of the name of the city pulled away from him. In it's place is the name "Weep".<br /><br />When a mythical hero, the Godslayer, arrives in town, Lazlo is able to join the group on their quest for Weep. This is his biggest dream come to life. He finally has a chance to see the legendary city that he's only fantasized about. <br /><br />What awaits Lazlo is more than he had imagined. Mythical beings, age-old grudges and a history that melded the worlds of gods and men. As more of Weep's past is unearthed, the brutality of the city's past is brought to light. Lazlo is forced to look at the city and it's inhabitants through a new lens.<br /><br />Although Lazlo was the central focus for much of this story, Ms. Taylor provides a robust cast of characters. Each member of this large cast brings something special to the story. I don't want to say too much for fear that I might spoil this story for others.<br /><br />Sarai is such a character. Her relationship with Lazlo is essential to the progression of the plot. From his dreams to his reality, Lazlo could not have found a better match than Sarai. They made each other better for having known one another. Their relationship was sweet and innocent, but also intense and emotional. I loved watching their bond evolve and seeing how their actions changed how they viewed the "outside" world. <br /><br />From start to finish, this was an entertaining and captivating story. Laini Taylor's writing is poetic. You can't help but notice the beauty of her prose.<br /><br />I listened to the Audible version of this book and it was well-narrated. My only criticism is that it was a bit hard to follow at first. This author's works are multifaceted and incredibly detailed. At first, this can be a bit difficult to follow when listening. I did have to rewind a few times in the beginning to keep my characters and events straight. However, I was able to get it all sorted out pretty soon and I wouldn't trade the richness of the story for the small amount of time lost. <br /><br />Overall, I thought that this was a wonderful story! I would definitely recommend it, whether you're a die-hard fan of paranormal/fantasy or if you're just an occasional dabbler, like me. Laini Taylor has created a fantastical and intriguing world. I am looking forward to seeing where this series will go.<br /><br />Check out more of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bookaddicthaven.com">www.bookaddicthaven.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1230755875123001021" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2555369267" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2555369267" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2555369267?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2555369267" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7143495078213501460"><b>So strange and terrible and lovely</b><br/><blockquote>
  <i>❝Dream up something wild and improbable. Something beautiful and full of monsters.❞</i>
</blockquote><br/>I finally get it. I get the shrines built for Laini Taylor, the adoration of her faithful fans, because after diving into her <b>whimsical and peculiar stories of boys and girls consumed by hunger, swallowing fairy tales and miracles and plums, dreaming big and loving tenderly and passionately,</b> <i>not</i> worshipping her is not an option. <u>It’s a reflective response.</u> I can’t tell you the</span>
  <span id="freeText7143495078213501460" style="display:none"><b>So strange and terrible and lovely</b><br /><blockquote>
  <i>❝Dream up something wild and improbable. Something beautiful and full of monsters.❞</i>
</blockquote><br />I finally get it. I get the shrines built for Laini Taylor, the adoration of her faithful fans, because after diving into her <b>whimsical and peculiar stories of boys and girls consumed by hunger, swallowing fairy tales and miracles and plums, dreaming big and loving tenderly and passionately,</b> <i>not</i> worshipping her is not an option. <u>It’s a reflective response.</u> I can’t tell you the exact moment I got lost in her words; I can only tell you that <b>I never recovered</b>.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>❝It was the first week of Twelfthmoon, on the far side of Elmuthaleth, and Strange the dreamer –library stowaway and scholar of fairy tales – had never been thirstier, or more full of wonder.❞</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>Full of wonder</b> is the perfect description of how I felt while reading Strange the Dreamer; full of <b>yearning</b>, of an insatiable need to taste and touch and feel the world Laini Taylor created. To live inside it, to savor it in my tongue and bask in the <b>otherworldliness and the warmth</b> that enveloped me. I was incorporeal, weightless, trailing behind Lazlo, flying among moths, smelling leather-bound tomes, strolling along colorful gardens, <b>torn between dreams and nightmares</b>. Blue skin, crimson blood, golden domes, were all I could see. I was ephemeral and eternal and I knew, with absolute clarity, that this <b>little piece of magic</b> will always hold a special place in my heart.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>❝The dream chooses the dreamer, not the other way around.❞</i>
</blockquote><br />Strange the Dreamer is the story of a librarian who was fortunate enough to accomplish his heart’s greatest desire; to see the mythic lost city of Weep, and to gather evidence of magic. It’s the story of the Muse of Nightmares, a girl banished from the world for the crimes of her mother, but found compassion for the ones who wronged her. It’s the story of a hero who was also a butcher. A golden son who could not grasp the concept of kindness. A girl who was stuck in the past and wished to avenge the dead by causing a second massacre. <b>It’s the story of gods and monsters and men, of heroic villains and villainous heroes, of pure love, heinous crimes and, in the end, acceptance.</b><br /><blockquote>
  <i>❝He read while he walked. He read while he ate. The other librarians suspected he somehow read while he slept, or perhaps didn't sleep at all.❞</i>
</blockquote><br />There is no character I have cherished more than <b>Lazlo Strange</b>; I <b>identified</b> with him, with the physical attraction to books and pages and lores and tales to the very marrow. His quest to find magic, his incline towards kindness instead of malice, they are some rare qualities that made him so precious. <b>Sarai</b>, with her understanding and her dream to belong in a world full of hatred and prejudice was also endearing. Every single character was portrayed in various shades, a blend of self-loathing, hatred, ambition, redemption and love coated them, leading them to horrible things and great acts of courage.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>❝I think you’re a fairy tale. I think you’re magical, and brave, and exquisite. And I hope you'll let me be in your story.❞</i>
</blockquote><br />Strange the Dreamer was <b>a remedy for the soul</b>; it inflicted wounds, painful and devastating wounds, but it did so in a delicate manner. You only have to discover it yourselves! <br /><br /> <a href="http://booknest.eu/reviews/kat/1362-strangethedreamer" rel="nofollow noopener">Review also posted on BookNest!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7143495078213501460" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
